</td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p>The <b>Mongol Empire</b> of the 13th and 14th centuries was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest contiguous land empire</a> in <a href="/wiki/Human_history" title="Human history">history</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[5]</a></sup> Originating in present-day <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, the Mongol Empire at its height stretched from the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a> to parts of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, extending northward into parts of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[6]</a></sup> eastward and southward into parts of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, attempted invasions of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and conquered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_Plateau" title="Iranian Plateau">Iranian Plateau</a>; and westward as far as the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>.
</p><p>The Mongol Empire emerged from the unification of several <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic tribes</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> homeland under the <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">leadership</a> of <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1162</span>–1227), whom a council proclaimed as the ruler of all Mongols in 1206. The empire grew rapidly under his rule and that of his descendants, who sent out <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions" title="Mongol invasions">invading armies</a> in every direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[8]</a></sup> The vast transcontinental empire connected the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">East</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">West</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>, in an enforced <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Mongolica" title="Pax Mongolica">Pax Mongolica</a></i>, allowing the exchange of trade, technologies, commodities and ideologies across <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>The empire began to split due to wars over succession, as the grandchildren of Genghis Khan disputed whether the royal line should follow from his son and initial heir <a href="/wiki/%C3%96gedei_Khan" title="Ögedei Khan">Ögedei</a> or from one of his other sons, such as <a href="/wiki/Tolui" title="Tolui">Tolui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khan" title="Chagatai Khan">Chagatai</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Jochi" title="Jochi">Jochi</a>. The Toluids prevailed after a bloody purge of Ögedeid and Chagatayid factions, but disputes continued among the descendants of Tolui. A key reason for the split was the dispute over whether the Mongol Empire would become a sedentary, cosmopolitan empire, or would stay true to the Mongol nomadic and steppe-based lifestyle. After <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Khan" title="Möngke Khan">Möngke Khan</a> died (1259), rival <a href="/wiki/Kurultai" title="Kurultai">kurultai</a> councils simultaneously elected different successors, the brothers <a href="/wiki/Ariq_B%C3%B6ke" title="Ariq Böke">Ariq Böke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, who fought each other in the <a href="/wiki/Toluid_Civil_War" title="Toluid Civil War">Toluid Civil War</a> (1260–1264) and also dealt with challenges from the descendants of other sons of Genghis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[12]</a></sup> Kublai successfully took power, but war ensued as he sought unsuccessfully to regain control of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Chagatai_Khans" title="List of Chagatai Khans">Chagatayid</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_of_%C3%96gedei" title="House of Ögedei">Ögedeid</a> families.
</p><p>During the reigns of Genghis and Ögedei, the Mongols suffered the occasional defeat when a less skilled general received the command. The Siberian <a href="/wiki/Tumed" title="Tumed">Tumeds</a> defeated the Mongol forces under <a href="/wiki/Borokhula" title="Borokhula">Borokhula</a> around 1215–1217; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jalal_ad-Din_Mingburnu" title="Jalal ad-Din Mingburnu">Jalal al-Din</a> defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shikhikhutug" title="Shikhikhutug">Shigi-Qutugu</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Parwan" title="Battle of Parwan">Battle of Parwan</a> in 1221; and the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin</a> generals Heda and Pu'a defeated Dolqolqu in 1230. In each case, the Mongols returned shortly after with a much larger army led by one of their best generals, and were invariably victorious. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ain_Jalut" title="Battle of Ain Jalut">Battle of Ain Jalut</a> in <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">Galilee</a> in 1260 marked the first time that the Mongols would not return to immediately avenge a defeat, due to a combination of the death of Möngke Khan in 1259, the Toluid Civil War between Ariq Böke and Kublai Khan, and <a href="/wiki/Berke" title="Berke">Berke Khan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> attacking <a href="/wiki/Hulagu_Khan" title="Hulagu Khan">Hulagu Khan</a> in Persia. Although the Mongols launched many more invasions of the Levant, briefly occupying it and raiding as far as <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a> after a decisive victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wadi_al-Khaznadar" title="Battle of Wadi al-Khaznadar">Battle of Wadi al-Khaznadar</a> in 1299, they withdrew due to various geopolitical factors.
</p><p>By the time of Kublai's death in 1294, the Mongol Empire had <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Division of the Mongol Empire">fractured into four separate khanates or empires</a>, each pursuing its own interests and objectives: the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> khanate in the northwest, the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a> in Central Asia, the <a href="/wiki/Ilkhanate" title="Ilkhanate">Ilkhanate</a> in the southwest, and the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreatYuan_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-GreatYuan-6">[note 3]</a></sup> in the east, based in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_p413_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-China_p413-21">[17]</a></sup> In 1304, during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Tem%C3%BCr_Khan" title="Temür Khan">Temür</a>, the three western khanates accepted <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> of the Yuan dynasty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>The part of the empire that fell first was the Ilkhanate which disintegrated in the period of 1335–1353. Next, the Yuan dynasty collapsed and lost control of <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a> in 1368 after its capital of <a href="/wiki/Khanbaliq" title="Khanbaliq">Dadu</a> was taken over by the <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han</a>-ruled <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a>. The Genghisid rulers of the Yuan then retreated north and continued to rule the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Plateau" title="Mongolian Plateau">Mongolian Plateau</a>. The regime is thereafter known as the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Yuan" title="Northern Yuan">Northern Yuan dynasty</a> in historiography. The Golden Horde had broken into competing khanates by the end of the 15th century and was defeated and thrown out of Russia in 1480 by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a> while the Chagatai Khanate lasted in one form or another until 1687.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<p>The Mongol Empire referred to itself as <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886223191" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr; vertical-align:text-top;">ᠶᠡᠬᠡ<br/>ᠮᠣᠩᠭᠣᠯ<br/>ᠤᠯᠤᠰ</span> <i>yeke Mongγol ulus</i> (<abbr title="literal translation">lit.</abbr> 'nation of the great Mongols' or the 'great Mongol nation') in Mongol or <i>kür uluγ ulus</i> (<abbr title="literal translation">lit.</abbr> the 'whole great nation') in Turkic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philology_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-philology-24">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the 1260 to 1264 <a href="/wiki/Toluid_Civil_War" title="Toluid Civil War">succession war</a> between <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a> and his brother <a href="/wiki/Ariq_B%C3%B6ke" title="Ariq Böke">Ariq Böke</a>, Kublai's power became limited to the eastern part of the empire, centred on China. Kublai officially issued an imperial <a href="/wiki/Edict" title="Edict">edict</a> on 18 December 1271 to name his realm Great Yuan (<i>Dai Yuan</i>, or <i>Dai Ön Ulus</i>) and to establish the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a>. Some sources give the full Mongol name as <i>Dai Ön Yehe Monggul Ulus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-empire_context">Pre-empire context</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Proto-Mongols" title="Proto-Mongols">Proto-Mongols</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongolia_XI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="830" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/250px-Mongolia_XI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/375px-Mongolia_XI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/500px-Mongolia_XI.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongolia_XI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mongol tribes during the Khitan <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a> (907–1125)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:East-Hem_1200ad.jpg"><img alt="Map of Eurasia showing the different states" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1903" data-file-width="3240" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/East-Hem_1200ad.jpg/250px-East-Hem_1200ad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/East-Hem_1200ad.jpg/375px-East-Hem_1200ad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/East-Hem_1200ad.jpg/500px-East-Hem_1200ad.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:East-Hem_1200ad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a> on the eve of the Mongol invasions, c. 1200</div></div></div>
<p>The area around <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a>, and parts of <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">North China</a> had been controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a> since the 10th century. In 1125, the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty</a> founded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jurchens" title="Jurchens">Jurchens</a> overthrew the Liao dynasty and attempted to gain control over former Liao territory in Mongolia. In the 1130s the Jin dynasty rulers, known as the Golden Kings, successfully resisted the <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a> confederation, ruled at the time by <a href="/wiki/Khabul_Khan" title="Khabul Khan">Khabul Khan</a>, great-grandfather of Genghis Khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barfield._p._184_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barfield._p._184-26">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongolian_plateau" title="Mongolian plateau">Mongolian plateau</a> was occupied mainly by five powerful tribal confederations (<i>khanlig</i>): <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naiman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merkit" title="Merkit">Mergid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tatar_confederation" title="Tatar confederation">Tatar</a>. The Jin emperors, following a policy of <a href="/wiki/Divide_and_rule" title="Divide and rule">divide and rule</a>, encouraged disputes among the tribes, especially between the Tatars and the Mongols, in order to keep the nomadic tribes distracted by their own battles and thereby away from the Jin. Khabul's successor was <a href="/wiki/Ambaghai" title="Ambaghai">Ambaghai Khan</a>, who was betrayed by the Tatars, handed over to the Jurchen, and executed. The Mongols retaliated by raiding the frontier, resulting in a failed Jurchen counter-attack in 1143.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barfield._p._184_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barfield._p._184-26">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1147, the Jin somewhat changed their policy, signing a peace treaty with the Mongols and withdrawing from a score of forts. The Mongols then resumed attacks on the Tatars to avenge the death of their late khan, opening a long period of active hostilities. The Jin and Tatar armies defeated the Mongols in 1161.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barfield._p._184_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Barfield._p._184-26">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the rise of the Mongol Empire in the 13th century, the usually cold, parched steppes of Central Asia enjoyed their mildest, wettest conditions in more than a millennium. It is thought that this resulted in a rapid increase in the number of war horses and other livestock, which significantly enhanced Mongol military strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_Genghis_Khan">Rise of Genghis Khan</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_Genghis_Khan" title="Rise of Genghis Khan">Rise of Genghis Khan</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg"><img alt="Painting of Genghis Khan" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1997" data-file-width="1578" decoding="async" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg/220px-YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg/330px-YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg/440px-YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumGenghisPortrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_Museum" title="National Palace Museum">National Palace Museum</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei,_Taiwan" title="Taipei, Taiwan">Taipei, Taiwan</a></div></div></div>
<p>Known during his childhood as Temüjin, Genghis Khan was a son of a Mongol chieftain. As a young man he rose very rapidly by working with Toghrul Khan of the Kerait. The most powerful Mongol leader at the time was Kurtait; he was given the Chinese title "Wang", which means King.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[24]</a></sup> Temujin went to war against Kurtait (now Wang Khan). After Temujin defeated Wang Khan he gave himself the name Genghis Khan. He then enlarged his Mongol state under himself and his kin. The term Mongol came to be used to refer to all Mongolic speaking tribes under the control of Genghis Khan. His most powerful allies were his father's friend, <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Khereid</a> chieftain <a href="/wiki/Toghrul" title="Toghrul">Toghrul</a>, and Temujin's childhood <i>anda</i> (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Blood_brother" title="Blood brother">blood brother</a>) <a href="/wiki/Jamukha" title="Jamukha">Jamukha</a> of the Jadran clan. With their help, Temujin defeated the Merkit tribe, rescued his wife Börte, and went on to defeat the Naimans and the Tatars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-29">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Temujin forbade looting of his enemies without permission, and he implemented a policy of sharing spoils with his warriors and their families instead of giving it all to the aristocrats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[26]</a></sup> These policies brought him into conflict with his uncles, who were also legitimate heirs to the throne; they regarded Temujin not as a leader but as an insolent usurper. This dissatisfaction spread to his generals and other associates, and some Mongols who had previously been allies broke their allegiance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-29">[25]</a></sup> War ensued, and Temujin and the forces still loyal to him prevailed, defeating the remaining rival tribes between 1203 and 1205 and bringing them under his sway. In 1206, Temujin was crowned as the <a href="/wiki/Khagan" title="Khagan">khagan</a> (Emperor) of the <i>Yekhe Mongol Ulus</i> (Great Mongol State) at a <a href="/wiki/Kurultai" title="Kurultai">Kurultai</a> (general assembly/council). It was there that he assumed the title of Genghis Khan (universal leader) instead of one of the old tribal titles such as Gur Khan or Tayang Khan, marking the start of the Mongol Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-29">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_organization">Early organization</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3088" data-file-width="2823" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg/220px-Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg/330px-Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg/440px-Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dschingis_Khan_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a> ascended the throne in the Ikh Khuraldai region in the Onan river, from the <a href="/wiki/Jami%27_al-tawarikh" title="Jami' al-tawarikh">Jami' al-tawarikh</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Genghis Khan introduced many innovative ways of organizing his army: for example dividing it into decimal subsections of arbans (10 soldiers), zuuns (100), <a href="/wiki/Mingghan" title="Mingghan">Mingghans</a> (1000), and <a href="/wiki/Tumen_(unit)" title="Tumen (unit)">tumens</a> (10,000). The <a href="/wiki/Kheshig" title="Kheshig">Kheshig</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_guard" title="Imperial guard">imperial guard</a>, was founded and divided into day (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khorchin" title="Khorchin">khorchin</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torghuds" title="Torghuds">torghuds</a>) and night (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khevtuul" title="Khevtuul">khevtuul</a>) guards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[27]</a></sup> Genghis rewarded those who had been loyal to him and placed them in high positions, as heads of army units and households, even though many of them came from very low-ranking clans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Secret_history._p._203_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Secret_history._p._203-32">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>Compared to the units he gave to his loyal companions, those assigned to his own family members were relatively few. He proclaimed a new code of law of the empire, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ikh_Zasag" title="Ikh Zasag">Ikh Zasag</a> or <a href="/wiki/Yassa" title="Yassa">Yassa</a>; later he expanded it to cover much of the everyday life and political affairs of the nomads. He forbade the selling of women, theft, fighting among the Mongols, and the hunting of animals during the breeding season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Secret_history._p._203_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Secret_history._p._203-32">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>He appointed his stepbrother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shikhikhutug" title="Shikhikhutug">Shikhikhutug</a> as supreme judge (jarughachi), ordering him to keep records of the empire. In addition to laws regarding family, food, and the army, Genghis also decreed religious freedom and supported domestic and international trade. He exempted the poor and the clergy from taxation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[29]</a></sup> He also encouraged literacy and the adaptation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uyghur_script" title="Uyghur script">Uyghur script</a> into what would become the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_script" title="Mongolian script">Mongolian script</a> of the empire, ordering the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uyghur_people" title="Uyghur people">Uyghur</a> <a href="/wiki/Tata-tonga" title="Tata-tonga">Tata-tonga</a>, who had previously served the khan of <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naimans</a>, to instruct his sons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Push_into_Central_Asia">Push into Central Asia</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Central_Asia" title="Mongol invasion of Central Asia">Mongol invasion of Central Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="813" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/220px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/330px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/440px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mongol Empire circa 1207</div></div></div>
<p>Genghis quickly came into conflict with the Jin dynasty of the Jurchens and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanguts" title="Tanguts">Tanguts</a> in northern China. He also had to deal with two other powers, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Tibet" title="Mongol invasions of Tibet">Tibet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qara_Khitai" title="Qara Khitai">Qara Khitai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before his death, Genghis Khan divided his empire among his sons and immediate family, making the Mongol Empire the joint property of the entire imperial family who, along with the Mongol aristocracy, constituted the ruling class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_policies">Religious policies</span></h4>
<p>Prior to the three western khanates' adoption of Islam, Genghis Khan and a number of his Yuan successors placed restrictions on religious practices they saw as alien. Muslims, including <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Hui</a>, and Jews, were collectively referred to as <i>Huihui</i>. Muslims were forbidden from <a href="/wiki/Islamic_dietary_laws" title="Islamic dietary laws">Halal</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dhabihah" title="Dhabihah"><i>Zabiha</i> butchering</a>, while Jews were similarly forbidden from <a href="/wiki/Kashrut" title="Kashrut">Kashrut</a> or <a href="/wiki/Shechita" title="Shechita"><i>Shehita</i> butchering</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[33]</a></sup> Referring to the conquered subjects as "our slaves," Genghis Khan demanded they no longer be able to refuse food or drink, and imposed restrictions on slaughter. Muslims had to slaughter sheep in secret.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>Among all the [subject] alien peoples only the Hui-hui say "we do not eat Mongol food". [Cinggis Qa’an replied:] "By the aid of heaven we have pacified you; you are our slaves. Yet you do not eat our food or drink. How can this be right?" He thereupon made them eat. "If you slaughter sheep, you will be considered guilty of a crime." He issued a regulation to that effect ... [In 1279/1280 under Qubilai] all the Muslims say: “if someone else slaughters [the animal] we do not eat". Because the poor people are upset by this, from now on, Musuluman [Muslim] Huihui and Zhuhu [Jewish] Huihui, no matter who kills [the animal] will eat [it] and must cease slaughtering sheep themselves, and cease the rite of circumcision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[35]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Genghis Khan arranged for the Chinese Taoist master <a href="/wiki/Qiu_Chuji" title="Qiu Chuji">Qiu Chuji</a> to visit him in Afghanistan, and also gave his subjects the right to religious freedom, despite his own shamanistic beliefs.
</p>
<h3><span id="Death_of_Genghis_Khan_and_expansion_under_.C3.96gedei_.281227.E2.80.931241.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Genghis_Khan_and_expansion_under_Ögedei_(1227–1241)">Death of Genghis Khan and expansion under Ögedei (1227–1241)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">Mongol invasions and conquests</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2006" data-file-width="1420" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg/220px-CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg/330px-CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg/440px-CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CoronationOfOgodei1229.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coronation of <a href="/wiki/%C3%96gedei_Khan" title="Ögedei Khan">Ögedei Khan</a> in 1229 as the successor of Genghis Khan. By <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rashid-al-Din_Hamadani" title="Rashid-al-Din Hamadani">Rashid al-Din</a>, early 14th century.</div></div></div>
<p>Genghis Khan died on 18 August 1227, by which time the Mongol Empire ruled from the Pacific Ocean to the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>, an empire twice the size of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> or the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphate</a> at their height.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Genghis named his third son, the charismatic <a href="/wiki/%C3%96gedei_Khan" title="Ögedei Khan">Ögedei</a>, as his heir. According to Mongol tradition, Genghis Khan was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tomb_of_Genghis_Khan" title="Tomb of Genghis Khan">buried in a secret location</a>. The regency was originally held by Ögedei's younger brother <a href="/wiki/Tolui" title="Tolui">Tolui</a> until Ögedei's formal election at the kurultai in 1229.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Among his first actions Ögedei sent troops to subjugate the <a href="/wiki/Bashkirs" title="Bashkirs">Bashkirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a>, and other nations in the Kipchak-controlled steppes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[37]</a></sup> In the east, Ögedei's armies re-established Mongol authority in Manchuria, crushing the <a href="/wiki/Puxian_Wannu" title="Puxian Wannu">Eastern Xia</a> regime and the <a href="/wiki/Tungusic_peoples" title="Tungusic peoples">Water Tatars</a>. In 1230, the great khan personally led his army in the campaign against the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty</a> of China. Ögedei's general <a href="/wiki/Subutai" title="Subutai">Subutai</a> captured the capital of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Aizong_of_Jin" title="Emperor Aizong of Jin">Wanyan Shouxu</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_siege_of_Kaifeng" title="Mongol siege of Kaifeng">siege of Kaifeng</a> in 1232.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[38]</a></sup> The Jin dynasty collapsed in 1234 when the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Caizhou" title="Siege of Caizhou">Mongols captured Caizhou</a>, the town to which Wanyan Shouxu had fled. In 1234, three armies commanded by Ögedei's sons Kochu and Koten and the <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tangut</a> general Chagan invaded southern China. With the assistance of the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> the Mongols finished off the Jin in 1234.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many Han Chinese and Khitan defected to the Mongols to fight against the Jin. Two Han Chinese leaders, <a href="/wiki/Shi_Tianze" title="Shi Tianze">Shi Tianze</a>, Liu Heima (劉黑馬, Liu Ni),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[41]</a></sup> and the Khitan Xiao Zhala defected and commanded the 3 Tumens in the Mongol army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[42]</a></sup> Liu Heima and Shi Tianze served Ogödei Khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[43]</a></sup> Liu Heima and Shi Tianxiang led armies against Western Xia for the Mongols.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[44]</a></sup> There were four Han Tumens and three Khitan Tumens, with each Tumen consisting of 10,000 troops. The Yuan dynasty created a Han army 漢軍 from Jin defectors, and another of ex-Song troops called the Newly Submitted Army 新附軍.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the West Ögedei's general <a href="/wiki/Chormaqan" title="Chormaqan">Chormaqan</a> destroyed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jalal_ad-Din_Mingburnu" title="Jalal ad-Din Mingburnu">Jalal ad-Din Mingburnu</a>, the last <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">shah</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_dynasty" title="Khwarazmian dynasty">Khwarizmian Empire</a>. The small kingdoms in southern Persia voluntarily accepted Mongol supremacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[47]</a></sup> In East Asia, there were a number of <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Korea" title="Mongol invasions of Korea">Mongol campaigns into Goryeo Korea</a>, but Ögedei's attempt to annex the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a> met with little success. <a href="/wiki/Gojong_of_Goryeo" title="Gojong of Goryeo">Gojong</a>, the king of <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo</a>, surrendered but later revolted and massacred Mongol <i><a href="/wiki/Darughachi" title="Darughachi">darughachis</a></i> (overseers); he then moved his imperial court from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaeseong" title="Gaeseong">Gaeseong</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ganghwa_Island" title="Ganghwa Island">Ganghwa Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Invasions_of_Kievan_Rus.27_and_central_China"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasions_of_Kievan_Rus'_and_central_China">Invasions of Kievan Rus' and central China</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Rus'">Mongol invasion of Rus'</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_China" title="Mongol invasion of China">Mongol invasion of China</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_India" title="Mongol invasions of India">Mongol invasions of India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Korea" title="Mongol invasions of Korea">Mongol invasions of Korea</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_Tibet" title="Mongol conquest of Tibet">Mongol conquest of Tibet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg"><img alt="Painting of a battle scene" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="926" data-file-width="694" decoding="async" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg/220px-Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg/330px-Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg/440px-Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sacking_of_Suzdal_by_Batu_Khan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The sack of <a href="/wiki/Suzdal" title="Suzdal">Suzdal</a> by <a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a> in 1238, <a href="/wiki/Miniature_(illuminated_manuscript)" title="Miniature (illuminated manuscript)">miniature</a> from a 16th-century chronicle</div></div></div>
<p>Meanwhile, in an offensive action against the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>, Mongol armies captured Siyang-yang, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a>, but did not secure their control over the conquered areas. The Song generals were able to recapture Siyang-yang from the Mongols in 1239. After the sudden death of Ögedei's son Kochu in Chinese territory the Mongols withdrew from southern China, although Kochu's brother Prince Koten invaded <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> immediately after their withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morgan-49_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-49-29">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a>, another grandson of Genghis Khan, overran the territories of the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Bulgaria" title="Volga Bulgaria">Bulgars</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, the Kypchaks, Bashkirs, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mordvin" title="Mordvin">Mordvins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chuvash_people" title="Chuvash people">Chuvash</a>, and other nations of the southern <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Steppe#Russian_Steppe" title="Eurasian Steppe">Russian steppe</a>. By 1237 the Mongols were encroaching upon <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Ryazan" title="Principality of Ryazan">Ryazan</a>, the first Kievan Rus' principality they were to attack. After a three-day siege involving fierce fighting, the Mongols captured the city and massacred its inhabitants. They then proceeded to destroy the army of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Principality_of_Vladimir" title="Grand Principality of Vladimir">Grand Principality of Vladimir</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Sit_River" title="Battle of the Sit River">Battle of the Sit River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32-53">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mongols captured the <a href="/wiki/Alania" title="Alania">Alania</a> capital <a href="/wiki/Maghas" title="Maghas">Maghas</a> in 1238. By 1240, all Kievan Rus' <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'">had fallen to the Asian invaders</a> except for a few northern cities. Mongol troops under Chormaqan in Persia <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Georgia_and_Armenia" title="Mongol invasions of Georgia and Armenia">connecting his invasion</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> with the invasion of Batu and Subutai, forced the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenian</a> nobles to surrender as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_May._Chormaqan._p._32-53">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giovanni_de_Plano_Carpini" title="Giovanni de Plano Carpini">Giovanni de Plano Carpini</a>, the pope's envoy to the Mongol great khan, travelled through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> in February 1246 and wrote:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>They [the Mongols] attacked Russia, where they made great havoc, destroying cities and fortresses and slaughtering men; and they laid siege to Kiev, the capital of Russia; after they had besieged the city for a long time, they took it and put the inhabitants to death. When we were journeying through that land we came across countless skulls and bones of dead men lying about on the ground. Kiev had been a very large and thickly populated town, but now it has been reduced almost to nothing, for there are at the present time scarce two hundred houses there and the inhabitants are kept in complete slavery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[50]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Despite the military successes, strife continued within the Mongol ranks. Batu's relations with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk" title="Güyük">Güyük</a>, Ögedei's eldest son, and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCri" title="Büri">Büri</a>, the beloved grandson of <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khan" title="Chagatai Khan">Chagatai Khan</a>, remained tense and worsened during Batu's victory banquet in southern Kievan Rus'. Nevertheless, Güyük and Buri could not do anything to harm Batu's position as long as his uncle Ögedei was still alive. Ögedei continued with <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_India" title="Mongol invasions of India">offensives into the Indian subcontinent</a>, temporarily investing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uchch" title="Uchch">Uchch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Multan" title="Multan">Multan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Delhi Sultanate</a> and stationing a Mongol overseer in <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[51]</a></sup> though the invasions into India eventually failed and were forced to retreat. In northeastern Asia, Ögedei agreed to end the conflict with <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo</a> by making it a client state and sent Mongol princesses to wed Goryeo princes. He then reinforced his <a href="/wiki/Kheshig" title="Kheshig">kheshig</a> with the Koreans through both diplomacy and military force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Push_into_central_Europe">Push into central Europe</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">Mongol invasion of Europe</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">advance into Europe</a> continued with Mongol invasions of Poland and Hungary. When the western flank of the Mongols plundered Polish cities, a European alliance among the <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravians</a>, and the Christian military orders of the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Hospitallers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" title="Teutonic Knights">Teutonic Knights</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">Templars</a> assembled sufficient forces to halt, although briefly, the Mongol advance <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Legnica" title="Battle of Legnica">at Legnica</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungarian</a> army, their <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croatian allies</a> and the Knights Templar were beaten by the Mongols at the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mohi" title="Battle of Mohi">Sajo River</a> on 11 April 1241. Before Batu's forces could continue on to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, news of Ögedei's death in December 1241 brought a halt to the invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weatherford._p._158_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weatherford._p._158-59">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup> As was customary in Mongol military tradition, all princes of Genghis's line had to attend the kurultai to elect a successor. Batu and his western Mongol army withdrew from Central Europe the next year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._p._104_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._p._104-61">[57]</a></sup> Today researchers doubt that Ögedei's death was the sole reason for the Mongols withdrawal. Batu did not return to Mongolia, so a new khan was not elected until 1246. Climatic and environmental factors, as well as the strong fortifications and castles of Europe, played an important role in the Mongols' decision to withdraw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Post-.C3.96gedei_power_struggles_.281241.E2.80.931251.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Ögedei_power_struggles_(1241–1251)">Post-Ögedei power struggles (1241–1251)</span></h3>
<p>Following the Great Khan Ögedei's death in 1241, and before the next kurultai, Ögedei's widow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C3%B6regene" title="Töregene">Töregene</a> took over the empire. She persecuted her husband's Khitan and Muslim officials and gave high positions to her own allies. She built palaces, cathedrals, and social structures on an imperial scale, supporting religion and education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._95_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._95-64">[60]</a></sup> She was able to win over most Mongol aristocrats to support Ögedei's son <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Khan" title="Güyük Khan">Güyük</a>. But Batu, ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>, refused to come to the kurultai, claiming that he was ill and that the climate was too harsh for him. The resulting stalemate lasted more than four years and further destabilized the unity of the empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._95_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._95-64">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="198" data-file-width="254" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg/220px-%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/88/%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%96.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a> consolidates the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a></div></div></div>
<p>When Genghis Khan's youngest brother <a href="/wiki/Tem%C3%BCge" title="Temüge">Temüge</a> threatened to seize the throne, Güyük came to Karakorum to try to secure his position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup> Batu eventually agreed to send his brothers and generals to the kurultai convened by Töregene in 1246. Güyük by this time was ill and alcoholic, but his campaigns in Manchuria and Europe gave him the kind of stature necessary for a great khan. He was duly elected at a ceremony attended by Mongols and foreign dignitaries from both within and without the empire — leaders of vassal nations, representatives from Rome, and other entities who came to the kurultai to show their respects and conduct diplomacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2593" data-file-width="495" decoding="async" height="524" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg/100px-LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg/150px-LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg/200px-LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LetterGuyugToInnocence.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Khan" title="Güyük Khan">Güyük Khan</a> demanding <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_IV" title="Pope Innocent IV">Pope Innocent IV</a>'s submission. The 1246 <a href="/wiki/Letter_from_G%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Khan_to_Pope_Innocent_IV" title="Letter from Güyük Khan to Pope Innocent IV">letter</a> was written in Persian.</div></div></div>
<p>Güyük took steps to reduce corruption, announcing that he would continue the policies of his father Ögedei, not those of Töregene. He punished Töregene's supporters, except for governor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arghun_the_Elder" title="Arghun the Elder">Arghun the Elder</a>. He also replaced young <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qara_H%C3%BCl%C3%ABg%C3%BC" title="Qara Hülëgü">Qara Hülëgü</a>, the khan of the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a>, with his favorite cousin <a href="/wiki/Yes%C3%BC_M%C3%B6ngke" title="Yesü Möngke">Yesü Möngke</a>, to assert his newly conferred powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-68">[64]</a></sup> He restored his father's officials to their former positions and was surrounded by Uyghur, <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naiman</a> and Central Asian officials, favoring <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> commanders who had helped his father conquer Northern China. He continued military operations in Korea, advanced into Song China in the south, and into Iraq in the west, and ordered an empire-wide census. Güyük also divided the Sultanate of Rum between <a href="/wiki/Kaykaus_II" title="Kaykaus II">Izz-ad-Din Kaykawus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kilij_Arslan_IV" title="Kilij Arslan IV">Rukn ad-Din Kilij Arslan</a>, though Kaykawus disagreed with this decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-68">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>Not all parts of the empire respected Güyük's election. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hashshashin" title="Hashshashin">Hashshashins</a>, former Mongol allies whose Grand Master Hasan Jalalud-Din had offered his submission to Genghis Khan in 1221, angered Güyük by refusing to submit. Instead he murdered the Mongol generals in Persia. Güyük appointed his best friend's father <a href="/wiki/Eljigidei" title="Eljigidei">Eljigidei</a> as chief commander of the troops in Persia and gave them the task of both reducing the strongholds of the <a href="/wiki/Nizari_Ismaili_state" title="Nizari Ismaili state">Nizari Ismailis</a> and conquering the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasids" title="Abbasids">Abbasids</a> at the center of the Islamic world, Iran and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-68">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Death_of_G.C3.BCy.C3.BCk_.281248.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Güyük_(1248)">Death of Güyük (1248)</span></h4>
<p>In 1248, Güyük raised more troops and suddenly marched westward from the Mongol capital of Karakorum. The reasoning was unclear. Some sources wrote that he sought to recuperate at his personal estate, Emyl; others suggested that he might have been moving to join Eljigidei to conduct a full-scale conquest of the Middle East, or possibly to make a surprise attack on his rival cousin Batu Khan in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atwood._p._213_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atwood._p._213-70">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Suspicious of Güyük's motives, <a href="/wiki/Sorghaghtani_Beki" title="Sorghaghtani Beki">Sorghaghtani Beki</a>, the widow of Genghis's son Tolui, secretly warned her nephew Batu of Güyük's approach. Batu had himself been traveling eastward at the time, possibly to pay homage, or perhaps with other plans in mind. Before the forces of Batu and Güyük met, Güyük, sick and worn out by travel, died en route at Qum-Senggir (Hong-siang-yi-eulh) in <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, possibly a victim of poison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atwood._p._213_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Atwood._p._213-70">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turtle-Karakorum.jpg"><img alt="Photograph of a field with a large stone tortoise" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="392" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Turtle-Karakorum.jpg/220px-Turtle-Karakorum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Turtle-Karakorum.jpg/330px-Turtle-Karakorum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Turtle-Karakorum.jpg/440px-Turtle-Karakorum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turtle-Karakorum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A stone turtle at the site of the Mongol capital, <a href="/wiki/Karakorum" title="Karakorum">Karakorum</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Güyük's widow <a href="/wiki/Oghul_Qaimish" title="Oghul Qaimish">Oghul Qaimish</a> stepped forward to take control of the empire, but she lacked the skills of her mother-in-law Töregene, and her young sons Khoja and Naku and other princes challenged her authority. To decide on a new great khan, Batu called a kurultai on his own territory in 1250. As it was far from the Mongol heartland, members of the Ögedeid and Chagataid families refused to attend. The kurultai offered the throne to Batu, but he rejected it, claiming he had no interest in the position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159-71">[67]</a></sup> Batu instead nominated <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Khan" title="Möngke Khan">Möngke</a>, a grandson of Genghis from his son Tolui's lineage. Möngke was leading a Mongol army in Russia, the northern Caucasus and Hungary. The pro-Tolui faction supported Batu's choice, and Möngke was elected; though given the kurultai's limited attendance and location, it was of questionable validity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159-71">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>Batu sent Möngke, under the protection of his brothers, <a href="/wiki/Berke" title="Berke">Berke</a> and Tukhtemur, and his son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sartaq" title="Sartaq">Sartaq</a> to assemble a more formal kurultai at Kodoe Aral in the heartland. The supporters of Möngke repeatedly invited Oghul Qaimish and the other major Ögedeid and Chagataid princes to attend the kurultai, but they refused each time. The Ögedeid and Chagataid princes refused to accept a descendant of Genghis's son Tolui as leader, demanding that only descendants of Genghis's son Ögedei could be great khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._159-71">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Rule_of_M.C3.B6ngke_Khan_.281251.E2.80.931259.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_of_Möngke_Khan_(1251–1259)">Rule of Möngke Khan (1251–1259)</span></h3>
<p>When Möngke's mother Sorghaghtani and their cousin <a href="/wiki/Berke" title="Berke">Berke</a> organized a second kurultai on 1 July 1251, the assembled throng proclaimed Möngke great khan of the Mongol Empire. This marked a major shift in the leadership of the empire, transferring power from the descendants of Genghis's son Ögedei to the descendants of Genghis's son Tolui. The decision was acknowledged by a few of the Ögedeid and Chagataid princes, such as Möngke's cousin <a href="/wiki/Kadan" title="Kadan">Kadan</a> and the deposed khan Qara Hülëgü, but one of the other legitimate heirs, Ögedei's grandson Shiremun, sought to topple Möngke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._103_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._103-72">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>Shiremun moved with his own forces toward the emperor's nomadic palace with a plan for an armed attack, but Möngke was alerted by his falconer of the plan. Möngke ordered an investigation of the plot, which led to a series of major trials all across the empire. Many members of the Mongol elite were found guilty and put to death, with estimates ranging from 77 to 300, though princes of Genghis's royal line were often exiled rather than executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._103_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._103-72">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>Möngke confiscated the estates of the Ögedeid and the Chagatai families and shared the western part of the empire with his ally Batu Khan. After the bloody purge, Möngke ordered a general amnesty for prisoners and captives, but thereafter the power of the great khan's throne remained firmly with the descendants of Tolui.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._103_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._103-72">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_reforms">Administrative reforms</span></h4>
<p>Möngke was a serious man who followed the laws of his ancestors and avoided alcoholism. He was tolerant of outside religions and artistic styles, leading to the building of foreign merchants' quarters, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist_monasteries" title="Buddhist monasteries">Buddhist monasteries</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mosques" title="Mosques">mosques</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_churches" title="Christian churches">Christian churches</a> in the Mongol capital. As construction projects continued, Karakorum was adorned with Chinese, European, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_architecture" title="Persian architecture">Persian architecture</a>. One famous example was a large silver tree with cleverly designed pipes that dispensed various drinks. The tree, topped by a triumphant angel, was crafted by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guillaume_Boucher&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guillaume Boucher (page does not exist)">Guillaume Boucher</a>, a Parisian goldsmith.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hulagu_Khan.jpg"><img alt="Stylized line drawing of Hulagu, seated and drinking from a bowl" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1241" data-file-width="830" decoding="async" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hulagu_Khan.jpg/220px-Hulagu_Khan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hulagu_Khan.jpg/330px-Hulagu_Khan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hulagu_Khan.jpg/440px-Hulagu_Khan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hulagu_Khan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hulagu" title="Hulagu">Hulagu</a>, Genghis Khan's grandson and founder of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Il-Khanate" title="Il-Khanate">Il-Khanate</a>. From a medieval Persian manuscript.</div></div></div>
<p>Although he had a strong Chinese contingent, Möngke relied heavily on Muslim and Mongol administrators and launched a series of economic reforms to make government expenses more predictable. His court limited government spending and prohibited nobles and troops from abusing civilians or issuing edicts without authorization. He commuted the contribution system to a fixed poll tax which was collected by imperial agents and forwarded to units in need.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allsen._p._280_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allsen._p._280-74">[70]</a></sup> His court also tried to lighten the <a href="/wiki/Tax" title="Tax">tax burden</a> on commoners by reducing tax rates. He also centralized control of monetary affairs and reinforced the guards at the postal relays. Möngke ordered an empire-wide census in 1252 that took several years to complete and was not finished until <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novgorod" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a> in the far northwest was counted in 1258.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allsen._p._280_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Allsen._p._280-74">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>In another move to consolidate his power, Möngke assigned his brothers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hulagu" title="Hulagu">Hulagu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kublai" title="Kublai">Kublai</a> to rule Persia and Mongol-held China respectively. In the southern part of the empire he continued his predecessors' struggle against the Song dynasty. In order to outflank the Song from three directions, Möngke dispatched Mongol armies under his brother Kublai to <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a>, and under his uncle Iyeku to subdue Korea and pressure the Song from that direction as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-68">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kublai conquered the <a href="/wiki/Dali_Kingdom" title="Dali Kingdom">Dali Kingdom</a> in 1253 after the Dali King Duan Xingzhi defected to the Mongols and helped them conquer the rest of <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a>. Möngke's general Qoridai stabilized his control over Tibet, inducing leading monasteries to submit to Mongol rule. Subutai's son Uryankhadai reduced the neighboring peoples of Yunnan to submission and went to war with the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/%C4%90%E1%BA%A1i_Vi%E1%BB%87t" title="Đại Việt">Đại Việt</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Tr%E1%BA%A7n_dynasty" title="Trần dynasty">Trần dynasty</a> in northern Vietnam in 1258, but they had to draw back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atwood-255_68-4"><a href="#cite_note-atwood-255-68">[64]</a></sup> The Mongol Empire tried to invade Đại Việt again in 1285 and 1287 but were defeated both times.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_invasions_of_the_Middle_East_and_Southern_China">New invasions of the Middle East and Southern China</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_the_Levant" title="Mongol invasions of the Levant">Mongol invasions of the Levant</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_China" title="Mongol invasion of China">Mongol invasion of China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">Siege of Baghdad (1258)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2786" data-file-width="4429" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg/220px-DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg/330px-DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg/440px-DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsFallOfBaghdad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mongol invasion of Baghdad</div></div></div>
<p>After stabilizing the empire's finances, Möngke once again sought to expand its borders. At kurultais in Karakorum in 1253 and 1258 he approved new invasions of the Middle East and <a href="/wiki/South_Central_China" title="South Central China">south China</a>. Möngke put Hulagu in overall charge of military and civil affairs in Persia, and appointed Chagataids and Jochids to join Hulagu's army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129-75">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Muslims from <a href="/wiki/Qazvin" title="Qazvin">Qazvin</a> denounced the menace of the <a href="/wiki/Nizari_Ismaili_state" title="Nizari Ismaili state">Nizari Ismailis</a>, a well-known sect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shiites" title="Shiites">Shiites</a>. The Mongol Naiman commander <a href="/wiki/Kitbuqa" title="Kitbuqa">Kitbuqa</a> began to assault several Ismaili fortresses in 1253, before Hulagu advanced in 1256. Ismaili Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Rukn_al-Din_Khurshah" title="Rukn al-Din Khurshah">Rukn al-Din Khurshah</a> surrendered in 1257 and was executed. All of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Ismaili_castles" title="List of Ismaili castles">Ismaili strongholds</a> in Persia were destroyed by Hulagu's army in 1257, except for <a href="/wiki/Gerdkuh" title="Gerdkuh">Girdkuh</a> which held out until 1271.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._129-75">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bagdad1258.jpg"><img alt="Colorful medieval depiction of a siege, showing the city of Baghdad surrounded by walls, and the Mongol army outside" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1464" data-file-width="2074" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/220px-Bagdad1258.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/330px-Bagdad1258.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bagdad1258.jpg/440px-Bagdad1258.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bagdad1258.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">Fall of Baghdad, 1258</a></div></div></div>
<p>The center of the Islamic Empire at the time was Baghdad, which had held power for 500 years but was suffering internal divisions. When its caliph <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Mustasim" title="Al-Mustasim">al-Mustasim</a> refused to submit to the Mongols, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Battle of Baghdad (1258)">Baghdad was besieged and captured</a> by the Mongols in 1258 and subjected to a merciless sack, an event considered one of the most catastrophic events in the history of Islam, and sometimes compared to the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Mecca_(683)" title="Siege of Mecca (683)">rupture of the Kaaba</a>. With the destruction of the Abbasid Caliphate, Hulagu had an open route to Syria and moved against the other Muslim powers in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._132_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._132-76">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>His army advanced toward <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ayyubid" title="Ayyubid">Ayyubid</a>-ruled Syria, capturing small local states en route. The sultan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Nasir_Yusuf" title="Al-Nasir Yusuf">Al-Nasir Yusuf</a> of the Ayyubids refused to show himself before Hulagu; however, he had accepted Mongol supremacy two decades earlier. When Hulagu headed further west, the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Armenia" title="Lesser Armenia">Armenians</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">Cilicia</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seljuks" title="Seljuks">Seljuks</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">Rum</a> and the Christian realms of <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Antioch" title="Principality of Antioch">Antioch</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tripoli" title="County of Tripoli">Tripoli</a> submitted to Mongol authority, joining them in their assault against the Muslims. While some cities surrendered without resisting, others, such as Mayafarriqin fought back; their populations were massacred and the cities were sacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._pp._132_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._pp._132-76">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Death_of_M.C3.B6ngke_Khan_.281259.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Möngke_Khan_(1259)">Death of Möngke Khan (1259)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MongolEmpire.jpg"><img alt="Map of Asia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="366" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/MongolEmpire.jpg/220px-MongolEmpire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/MongolEmpire.jpg/330px-MongolEmpire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/MongolEmpire.jpg/440px-MongolEmpire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MongolEmpire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The extent of the Mongol Empire after the death of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Khan" title="Möngke Khan">Möngke Khan</a> (reigned 1251–1259).</div></div></div>
<p>Meanwhile, in the northwestern portion of the empire, Batu's successor and younger brother Berke sent punitive expeditions to <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>. Dissension began brewing between the northwestern and southwestern sections of the Mongol Empire as Batu suspected that Hulagu's invasion of Western Asia would result in the elimination of Batu's own dominance there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the southern part of the empire, Möngke Khan himself led his army, but did not complete the conquest of China. Military operations were generally successful, but prolonged, so the forces did not withdraw to the north as was customary when the weather turned hot. Disease ravaged the Mongol forces with bloody epidemics, and Möngke died there on 11 August 1259. This event began a new chapter in the history of the Mongols, as again a decision needed to be made on a new great khan. Mongol armies across the empire withdrew from their campaigns to convene a new kurultai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disunity">Disunity</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dispute_over_succession">Dispute over succession</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1150" data-file-width="1648" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg/220px-DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg/330px-DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg/440px-DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DiezAlbumsArmedRiders_II.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Mongols at war</div></div></div>
<p>Möngke's brother Hulagu broke off his successful military advance into Syria, withdrawing the bulk of his forces to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughan" title="Mughan">Mughan</a> and leaving only a small contingent under his general <a href="/wiki/Kitbuqa" title="Kitbuqa">Kitbuqa</a>. The opposing forces in the region, the Christian Crusaders and Muslim Mamluks, both recognizing that the Mongols were the greater threat, took advantage of the weakened state of the Mongol army and engaged in an unusual passive truce with each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138-79">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1260, the Mamluks advanced from Egypt, being allowed to camp and resupply near the Christian stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, and engaged Kitbuqa's forces just north of Galilee at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ain_Jalut" title="Battle of Ain Jalut">Battle of Ain Jalut</a>. The Mongols were defeated, and Kitbuqa executed. This pivotal battle marked the western limit for Mongol expansion in the Middle East, and the Mongols were never again able to make serious military advances farther than Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._The_Mongols._p._138-79">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a separate part of the empire, <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, another brother of Hulagu and Möngke, heard of the great khan's death at the Huai River in China. Rather than returning to the capital, he continued his advance into the <a href="/wiki/Wuchang_District" title="Wuchang District">Wuchang</a> area of China, near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a>. Their younger brother <a href="/wiki/Ariq_B%C3%B6ke" title="Ariq Böke">Ariqboke</a> took advantage of the absence of Hulagu and Kublai, and used his position at the capital to win the title of great khan for himself, with representatives of all the family branches proclaiming him as the leader at the kurultai in Karakorum. When Kublai learned of this, he summoned his own kurultai at <a href="/wiki/Kaiping" title="Kaiping">Kaiping</a>, and nearly all the senior princes and great <a href="/wiki/Noyan" title="Noyan">noyans</a> in North China and Manchuria supported his own candidacy over that of Ariqboke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan._p._104_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan._p._104-61">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mongol_Civil_War">Mongol Civil War</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Toluid_Civil_War" title="Toluid Civil War">Toluid Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berke%E2%80%93Hulagu_war" title="Berke–Hulagu war">Berke–Hulagu war</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3200" data-file-width="2678" decoding="async" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg/220px-YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg/330px-YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg/440px-YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YuanEmperorAlbumKhubilaiPortrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>'s grandson and founder of the Yuan dynasty</div></div></div>
<p>Battles ensued between the armies of Kublai and those of his brother Ariqboke, which included forces still loyal to Möngke's previous administration. Kublai's army easily eliminated Ariqboke's supporters and seized control of the civil administration in southern Mongolia. Further challenges took place from their cousins, the Chagataids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wassaf_p._12_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wassaf_p._12-80">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._109_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._109-81">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488-82">[78]</a></sup> Kublai sent Abishka, a Chagataid prince loyal to him, to take charge of Chagatai's realm. But Ariqboke captured and then executed Abishka, having his own man <a href="/wiki/Alghu" title="Alghu">Alghu</a> crowned there instead. Kublai's new administration blockaded Ariqboke in Mongolia to cut off food supplies, causing a famine. Karakorum fell quickly to Kublai, but Ariqboke rallied and re-took the capital in 1261.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wassaf_p._12_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wassaf_p._12-80">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson._p._109_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson._p._109-81">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barthold._Turkestan._p._488-82">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>In southwestern Ilkhanate, Hulagu was loyal to his brother Kublai, but clashes with their cousin Berke, a Muslim and the ruler of the Golden Horde, began in 1262. The suspicious deaths of Jochid princes in Hulagu's service, unequal distribution of war booty, and Hulagu's massacres of Muslims increased the anger of Berke, who considered supporting a rebellion of the Georgian Kingdom against Hulagu's rule in 1259–1260.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[79]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed.
